## Domain Knowledge (LLM-generated)
**Domain**: nonlinear dynamics / classical mechanics
**Analysis**: This task models the acceleration of a nonlinear harmonic oscillator, where dv_dt depends on restoring forces (functions of x), damping forces (functions of v), and possibly external driving forces (functions of t). The nonlinearity can appear in the spring term, damping term, or both.

**Common formula structures in this domain**:
- Simple harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x (linear restoring force)
- Damped harmonic oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v (linear restoring + linear damping)
- Duffing oscillator (undriven): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 (cubic nonlinear restoring force)
- Duffing oscillator (damped): dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v (cubic spring + linear damping)
- Driven Duffing oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * cos(c4 * t) (cubic spring + damping + harmonic drive)
- Van der Pol oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * (1 - c2 * x**2) * v (nonlinear damping)
- Quintic nonlinear oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * x**5 (higher-order nonlinearity)
- Softening/hardening spring with damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 + c2 * x**3 + c3 * v
- Nonlinear damping: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * v * abs(v) (quadratic velocity damping)
- Driven damped oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * v + c2 * sin(c3 * t) (linear oscillator with periodic forcing)
- Parametric oscillator: dv_dt = c0 * x * cos(c1 * t) (time-varying stiffness)
- Coupled nonlinear terms: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**2 * v + c2 * v (position-dependent damping)
- Generalized Duffing-Van der Pol: dv_dt = c0 * x + c1 * x**3 + c2 * v + c3 * x**2 * v + c4 * cos(c5 * t)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Odd-power restoring forces (x, x**3, x**5) preserve symmetry of oscillation about equilibrium, indicating symmetric potential wells
- Even-power position terms (x**2) in restoring force break symmetry, indicating asymmetric potential wells
- Position-dependent damping terms like x**2 * v indicate amplitude-dependent energy dissipation (Van der Pol type behavior)
- Sinusoidal or cosinusoidal functions of time indicate external periodic driving forces; frequency ratios determine resonance behavior
- Negative linear damping (positive coefficient of v) combined with nonlinear damping (x**2 * v) produces self-sustained limit cycle oscillations
- Cubic position terms with same sign as linear term produce hardening springs; opposite sign produces softening springs with potential escape
- Absence of explicit time dependence indicates autonomous system where energy is either conserved or monotonically dissipated
- Products of position and time-dependent terms (x * cos(c*t)) indicate parametric excitation rather than direct forcing

Let me verify candidates with `v**c` terms - could `v**c` somehow equal `v*exp(-|v|)`? No, because `v**c = v^c` is a power law while `v*exp(-|v|)` has exponential decay.

None of these can produce `v*exp(-|v|)`.

The critical observation is that `v*exp(-|v|)` is a very specific non-algebraic, non-polynomial function of v that cannot be represented by any of the building blocks available in the candidates (polynomials in v, powers `v**c`, `log`, `sin`, rational functions of v, `exp(c*v)`).

Therefore, no candidate can exactly match the GT.

After thorough analysis, none of the 50 candidates can be made mathematically equivalent to the ground truth expression because none can produce the `v*exp(-|v|)` term.
